## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: constitutive modeling / thermomechanical materials science
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature constitutive relationship of a material, where stress depends on strain (mechanical loading) and temperature (thermal effects including softening, stiffening, or phase transitions). The interplay between ε and T suggests thermoplastic, thermoelastic, or viscoplastic behavior.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic regime, small strains)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening/stiffening)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (strain hardening in plastic regime)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic transition)
- Johnson-Cook strength model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (flow stress with strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Thermal softening power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 + c2 * T)**c3 (combined strain hardening and thermal effects)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (elastic modulus with Arrhenius-type thermal dependence)
- Neo-Hookean rubber elasticity: sigma = c0 * T * (epsilon + c1 - c2 * (epsilon + c3)**(-2)) (entropic elasticity proportional to T)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elastic or hyperelastic model)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon))) * (1 + c3 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal correction)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power-law for pre-strained materials)
- Entropic elasticity: sigma = c0 * T * epsilon (stress proportional to both T and strain, rubber-like)
- Hyperbolic sine creep/flow: sigma = c0 * T * sinh(c1 * epsilon) (nonlinear stress-strain for polymers or high-T metals)
- Tanh saturation model: sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) * (1 + c2 * T) (saturating stress with thermal dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Entropic elasticity (rubbers, polymers) → stress proportional to absolute temperature: sigma ~ T * f(epsilon)
- Thermal softening in metals → multiplicative factor (1 - c*(T/Tm)**m) or (1 + c*T) reducing stress at high T
- Strain hardening → power-law or logarithmic dependence on strain: epsilon**n or log(1 + c*epsilon)
- Yield stress + hardening → additive constant plus nonlinear strain function: c0 + c1*epsilon**c2
- Phase transitions or sigmoidal stress-strain → tanh(c*epsilon) or similar sigmoid in strain
- Hyperelastic materials → odd polynomial in strain (epsilon, epsilon**3, epsilon**5) ensuring antisymmetry
- Creep/viscoplastic flow at high temperature → sinh or exponential functions of stress or strain with Arrhenius T-dependence
- Saturation hardening → exponential approach: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)) representing dislocation saturation
